        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3556295522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5799220419272849251"><b>4.25 “Woman of day” and “Prince of night” stars</b> 🌟<br/>✨<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600526989i/30127647._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <blockquote>
  <b> “I’m not human, wife,” he whispered into the darkness.<br/>“But you’re still mine, husband.” </b>
</blockquote> Radiance is the story of a human Ildiko, the Gauri king's niece and Brishen, the second Kai prince who have been thrust into an arranged union in order to forge an alliance between the Gaur and Kai kingdoms. <br/><br/>Their arrangement would not have been such a big deal if they didn't belong to totally different species and differ so vastly in appearance.<br/><br/><b> She tr</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5799220419272849251" style="display:none"><b>4.25 “Woman of day” and “Prince of night” stars</b> 🌟<br>✨<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600526989i/30127647._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b> “I’m not human, wife,” he whispered into the darkness.<br>“But you’re still mine, husband.” </b>
</blockquote> Radiance is the story of a human Ildiko, the Gauri king's niece and Brishen, the second Kai prince who have been thrust into an arranged union in order to forge an alliance between the Gaur and Kai kingdoms. <br><br>Their arrangement would not have been such a big deal if they didn't belong to totally different species and differ so vastly in appearance.<br><br><b> She traced the bridge of his nose and the line of one cheekbone. “You know, except for the gray skin, black nails and the one glowing eye looking at me, I could almost mistake you for Gauri.” He gave her a sleepy grin. She paled and frowned at him. “And then you smile,” she said. “Bursin’s wings, that’s a blood-curdling sight to wake up to at any time of the day.” <br>Brishen chuckled between her fingers as she tried to press his lips closed. “You won’t exactly be honored as the greatest beauty in all of Bast-Haradis, wife.” </b><br><br>Let me just say this: <u>I have never read a book where both the MCs are so mutually respectful of each other</u>! Inspite of being royal, both Ildiko and Brishen have been kind of unimportant their whole lives, and as such, they find kindred spirits in one another.<br><br><b>
  <i>Theirs was an agreement based on the beginnings of friendship, respect and an intuitive understanding of each other.</i>
</b><br><br>This is the story of how they deal with the court politics, invasions from the neighbouring kingdoms, and most importantly their feelings for each other!<br><br>I loved their banter, chemistry and gradual evolvement from friends to lovers. <br><br><i> Seeing them go from this: </i><br><br><b> “You find me ugly, don’t you?”<br>“Hideous,” he said. “A hag of a woman. And you, “You don’t think me a handsome man?”<br>“Had you crawled out from under my bed when I was a child, I would have bludgeoned you to death with my father’s mace.” </b><br><br><i> To this:</i><br><br><b> “What do you think of your dead eel in the daylight?”<br>Ildiko brushed a feathery strand of his hair away from his eyes. “He pleases me greatly. The handsomest of eels.” His high cheekbones angled sharply under her palms. “So says this hag.”<br>“Who is most beautiful in the darkness.” Brishen kissed her then. </b><br><br><i> It was so heartwarming! </i> ♡<br><br>Now, let's talk about a different character: <u>the Kai Queen Secmis AKA Brishen's mother AKA bitchiest-mom-in-law ever</u>! At first, we just see her passing snide remarks about Ildiko whenever she got the chance, and I really enjoyed how Ildiko gave her fitting replies!<br><br><b> “You humans are very pale,” she said. “Only our diseased sport that shade.”<br>Ildiko sipped soup from her spoon, offering no indication that either the soup’s taste or Secmis’s comment bothered her. She dabbed at her lips with her sanap before answering. “You’re right, your Majesty; we are quite pale by comparison. The Kai are very gray. Only our dead are that color.” </b><br><br>You go, girl! However, it wasn't until one of Brishen's childhood memory was revealed that I hated her with a passion. That lady is *<i>pure evil</i>* and deserves to rot in hell.<br><br>Even though the writing took a while for me to get into, I really liked this book.<br><br><b>Radiance</b> doesn't exactly end with a cliffhanger, the epilogue is just foreshadowing for the next book. It was scary, but is it wrong to say it also soothed my soul?<br><br>Needless to say, I'll definitely read the next book because Ildiko and Brishen were *<u>everything</u>*.<br><br><blockquote> <b> She continued to stare at him. “What is it, Ildiko?” he asked. “What do you see?”<br>She twined her arms around his neck and tilted her head until her lips brushed the corner of his mouth. “My beautiful husband.” she said. “I see radiance.”<br><br>“Woman of day,” he said slowly. “You mean everything to me.” </b> </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5799220419272849251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1318310121" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1318310121" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1318310121?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=4-stars-romance-or-smut">4-stars-romance-or-smut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=dis-is-a-rully-good-lurv-story">dis-is-a-rully-good-lurv-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1318310121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17023808298345281478"><b>Maybe more like 3.5 stars, but I'll round up for the reasons below.</b><br/><br/>This is an unfolding love story in a fantasy setting. Bristen is a member of the royal Kai family and heir to the throne, but far enough down the chain that he will never be king. Ildiko is the young noblewoman he is arranged to marry, whose only worth is being married off in a political alliance.<br/><br/>They discover they actually like each other - as friends. This is sort of a vague Beauty and the Beast re-telling, only both people vie</span>
  <span id="freeText17023808298345281478" style="display:none"><b>Maybe more like 3.5 stars, but I'll round up for the reasons below.</b><br><br>This is an unfolding love story in a fantasy setting. Bristen is a member of the royal Kai family and heir to the throne, but far enough down the chain that he will never be king. Ildiko is the young noblewoman he is arranged to marry, whose only worth is being married off in a political alliance.<br><br>They discover they actually like each other - as friends. This is sort of a vague Beauty and the Beast re-telling, only both people view the other as the beast. To Brishen, Ildiko's human eyes look like separate disgusting entities, parasites, moving around in her head. To Ildiko, Brishen is the stuff nightmares are made of, with his gray skin, long claws, a mouth full of sharp teeth, and glowing eyes.. <br><br>But they appreciate each others honesty, humor, and intelligence, so they form a friendship and try to make the best of their marriage. Of course, since this is a romance, stuff happens, and things change.<br><br>I enjoyed the world-building in this. The Kai people were interesting to read about. I really appreciated the fact that there was no "virgin trope," which most romances seem to have. Also, the two leads were friends first, and their platonic relationship was believable. Neither character was annoying or did stupid things. Again, that is always refreshing. <br><br>If you are looking for a more relaxed (slow-paced) intelligent fantasy romance with a slowly evolving relationship, this is for you. There is a dash of magic, although it was a bit under-developed, in my view. The ending is a bit of a cliffhanger, but nothing major. I am definitely interested in seeing what happens next in this world. <br><br><b>Review also found at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theparanormalpaladin.wordpress.com/">https://theparanormalpaladin.wordpres...</a> <br><br>Original post:</b><br><br><i>Buddy read with my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo</a> freakazoids. <br><br>I don't do fantasy romance very often, but this one looks like my kind of thing.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385891201ra/7251779.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17023808298345281478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1203577725" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203577725" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203577725?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203577725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7387290661568751930">I probably never would have picked up this book if not for the glowing recommendations of some of my trusted fellow bloggers. I know that you're not supposed to judge a book by its cover, but the sad fact is, sometimes I guess I do. And if I would have ignored this book, I would have really missed out on a great fantasy romance.<br/><br/>This is my very first book by Grace Draven. The good news about that is, if this story is any indication, I'm going to have a grand time rolling around in her backlist. D</span>
  <span id="freeText7387290661568751930" style="display:none">I probably never would have picked up this book if not for the glowing recommendations of some of my trusted fellow bloggers. I know that you're not supposed to judge a book by its cover, but the sad fact is, sometimes I guess I do. And if I would have ignored this book, I would have really missed out on a great fantasy romance.<br /><br />This is my very first book by Grace Draven. The good news about that is, if this story is any indication, I'm going to have a grand time rolling around in her backlist. Draven has created two interesting and likeable characters, who fall in love against the odds. It is a slow burn, but all the more satisfying for it... because I believed in it, which is no small task considering the circumstances.<br /><br />Ildiko and Brishen are both expendable members of their respective royal families. Their marriage was cultivated as a political alliance. That wouldn't be a big deal except that they are from different species who find each other hideous. Though each of them is considered good looking by their own people, they are entirely unappealing to one another --at least in the physical sense. Fortunately, these two are able to look past that. Brishen sees the political aplomb, courage, and humor in his new wife, as Ildiko sees the honor, integrity and strength in him. It's inside the bonds of a growing friendship and mutual respect that romance blooms.<br /><br />The world building here is very well done. It's an alien landscape, but Draven sets it up as naturally as breathing. We really learn our hero and heroine best when it's against the backdrop of their families and cultures.<br /><br />There are also plenty of things happening to keep the plot moving. There are political machinations, assassination attempts, and ancient magics. But at the core, this a romance, and one I adored. I loved the way Ildiko and Brished treated one another. I loved that they were ugly to one another, until they were not. I loved the intensity of their intimacy, once it entered the picture. In fact, I can't think of anything I didn't like, except that it ended leaving me feeling like there should have been more. I walked away feeling a little incomplete, but I guess that guarantees I'll be back for more when <i>Eidolon </i>(book 2) comes out.<br /><br />Rating: A-</span>
  <a data-text-id="7387290661568751930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183907027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13524010025293945137">Actual Rating is 3.5 stars<br/><br/>This book was so unbelievably cute. I either smiled or cooed when I was reading it. The relationship between Brishen and Ildiko was just so amazing. They were really honest with each other and I appreciated that. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>”She hadn’t chosen this husband of hers, nor had he chosen her, but fate or kind gods had brought them together, made them friends and then lovers.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Since this story gave a premise of an arranged marriage, I went into it expecting a lot of arguing, angst and</span>
  <span id="freeText13524010025293945137" style="display:none">Actual Rating is 3.5 stars<br /><br />This book was so unbelievably cute. I either smiled or cooed when I was reading it. The relationship between Brishen and Ildiko was just so amazing. They were really honest with each other and I appreciated that. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>”She hadn’t chosen this husband of hers, nor had he chosen her, but fate or kind gods had brought them together, made them friends and then lovers.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Since this story gave a premise of an arranged marriage, I went into it expecting a lot of arguing, angst and hatred between the two MC’s but they were surprisingly mature about the situation and that's one of the reasons I liked this book.<br /><br />The characters were okay, I liked them enough and found that they had personalities but not that much, I hope they develop more in the second.<br /><br />The writing was good as well, It was easy to get into and not at all confusing.<br />Am still confused about how to rate this book, but it ranges from 3.5 to 4 stars I guess?<br /><br />While I found the romance cute, I wanted more politics and maybe a little more death<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Brishen was kidnapped, I expected the action to last a little longer cause it was so short. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Another reason I didn't give this book 5 stars is because they seemed to talk about some stuff in past tense when it has already happened. I would've preferred if it was narrated from the present.<br /><br />I would recommend this to people looking for a romance that's not cheesy but still cute.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7050261806749817858">I think we all know how hyped this book is. Because of that, I had such high expectations going into this one. That, plus the fact that I just read From Blood and Ash by Jennifer L Armtentrout and was BLOWN AWAY by that book, Radiance just didn't live up to the expectations I had. <br/><br/>When I started this book, I honestly thought it was going to be a new favorite of mine. The two main characters are revolted by one another, but they got along really well. I loved how they just kind of clicked persona</span>
  <span id="freeText7050261806749817858" style="display:none">I think we all know how hyped this book is. Because of that, I had such high expectations going into this one. That, plus the fact that I just read From Blood and Ash by Jennifer L Armtentrout and was BLOWN AWAY by that book, Radiance just didn't live up to the expectations I had. <br /><br />When I started this book, I honestly thought it was going to be a new favorite of mine. The two main characters are revolted by one another, but they got along really well. I loved how they just kind of clicked personality-wise and enjoyed one another's company and being honest with each other. The romance, though, was soooooooo slow and pair that with a super slow plot and I had a hard time getting through this book. There was a lot of sitting around and talking, eating dinner, and sitting around and talking. Where's the magic??? Brishen has some sort of magical ability, but he barely even used that. <br /><br />The end of the book did pick up, but the epilogue took the story in an entirely new direction and I'm not sure if I'll like it. The romance is already established, so the plot is going to have to really step it up in book two for me to enjoy it, if I end up picking it up. This romance was super cute with how they were friends and slowly realized they actually were attracted to each other first emotionally and then physically, but I need more substance to my fantasy romances to enjoy them. </span>

<div id="review_2651512595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2651512595" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2651512595?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11475773-charlotte?shelf=women-and-nb-of-speculative-fiction">women-and-nb-of-speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2651512595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer380291673811684238"><i>“Woman of day,” he said slowly. “You mean everything to me.”</i><br/><br/>I swear I’m still reading fantasy books! Today’s book is <i>Radiance</i> by Grace Draven, her 2014 romance. Spoilers follow, as well as mentions of sexual violence and torture.<br/><br/><b>What I Thought</b><br/><br/>A not-so-secret fact about me is that I’m a strange mix of jaded cynicism and sappy puppy eyes when it comes to fictional romances. When I fall for a couple I fall hard, but it takes a lot for me to fall in the first place. If you’ve been following my revie</span>
  <span id="freeText380291673811684238" style="display:none"><i>“Woman of day,” he said slowly. “You mean everything to me.”</i><br /><br />I swear I’m still reading fantasy books! Today’s book is <i>Radiance</i> by Grace Draven, her 2014 romance. Spoilers follow, as well as mentions of sexual violence and torture.<br /><br /><b>What I Thought</b><br /><br />A not-so-secret fact about me is that I’m a strange mix of jaded cynicism and sappy puppy eyes when it comes to fictional romances. When I fall for a couple I fall hard, but it takes a lot for me to fall in the first place. If you’ve been following my reviews at all, you’ve probably heard me say “I didn’t care at all about the love story. NEXT!!” quite often. I started this book hoping that <i>Radiance</i> would join <i>Heart’s Blood</i> and <i>Empire of Sand</i> as one of the swooniest romances I’ve read for this reading challenge. My ultimate verdict is that there were things I loved about this story but a number of other elements served to drag my enjoyment down quite a bit.<br /><br />When I was jotting down notes for this review, the first thing I wrote was “Where’s the conflict?” My problem, for the record, is not that Brishen and Idilko get along so well- as I’ll discuss later, this was delightful to me. The thing is that while the relationship itself doesn’t serve as a source of conflict or tension in the story, nothing else really does either. There are little spurts of plot and then one intense cascade into crazy violence at the end, but for the most part Brishen and Idilko face no compelling challenges, external or internal. I vastly prefer a romance where the couple has something or other to overcome together to one where they face no real demands for the majority of the book.<br /><br />I think you could make the argument that the book’s main source of conflict/plot is the two of them learning to overcome their differences, but I had some quibbles with Draven’s way of going about this too. For one thing, the distrust and fear between the humans and the Kai is just so bizarrely predicated on physical appearances alone, with very little exploration of underlying prejudices and stereotypes about culture, religion, social mores or personal characteristics other than eyes and skin color. There are times when other, deeper, differences are touched on, to be sure, but these are few and far between compared to the endless surface-level reflections on how different the Kai and humans look.<br /><br />Another part of my problem here could be that for the most part Brishen and Idilko don’t significantly struggle to adapt. Idilko, especially, changes her entire life with remarkable equanimity, and while this flexibility is a commendable trait I think I’d find more significant culture shock to be more engaging. Another quibble is that most of the differences between the Kai and humans simply become a matter of joking banter between the main couple, with the same three or four jokes repeated into infinity in a rather tiresome way: yes, their people find each other ugly! Potatoes and scarpatine pie! Idilko looks scary when she crosses her eyes!<br /><br />Intentional humor aside, there is also the matter of a few decisions that left me laughing even though I’m not sure they were supposed to. For one thing, what is the deal with Brishen’s preoccupation with rape? At one point Idilko tells him that she’s had sex before and immediately, apropos of absolutely nothing that she has said, he’s like WAS IT RAPE????? Like, what? Why would you think that? Shortly thereafter they have sex for the first time and right before the sex scene starts he’s all like “I’ve never raped anyone before and I never will!!!!!!” Okay, good for you, I guess? Gold star? I think what he’s trying to do is check for consent, but I’m stumped as to why Draven framed it that way. You all know that I get mad about poorly-handled rape stuff at the drop of a HAT, but none of this necessarily makes me mad- it’s just bizarre.<br /><br />Okay, the other amazing thing that happens with Brishen is that towards the end of the story he gets kidnapped and tortured, and part of that torture involves his clawlike fingernails getting ripped off. What’s absolutely extraordinary is that the first thing he thinks about his torture when we next get his perspective is “Well, at least I can finger Idilko safely now!” lololol. There are two wolves inside of me…one of them wants to get all righteously indignant at how dismissively his trauma was handled, but the other one is just like “You know what? What an absolute KING, an icon. Honestly, God bless this man.”<br /><br /><b>The F Word</b><br /><br />This is the story of two nice and good people who like each other right away and quickly become friends before also falling in love. They enjoy spending time together, there are heaps of mutual regard and respect, everything sexual that happens is 100% consensual and they truly face the world as equal partners who are ready to help each other and learn from each other. It’s just….nice and pure and good, and a delightful change of pace from a lot of the other romances I’ve read for this challenge. For all the time I’ve spent yelling about unhealthy relationships, I’d be totally remiss if I didn’t also laud the positive examples that I come across, and this is certainly one of the best.<br /><br />As for the nature of the gender dynamics in this book, I’m not quite sure what to say. There’s a clear division between Brishen’s responsibilities as warrior prince and Idilko’s responsibilities as his non-warrior wife, although one of my favorite characters is a female warrior cousin of Brishen’s who demonstrates that the Kai’s gender roles are much more flexible than the humans’. I’m not one of those people who thinks that it’s automatically antifeminist to write about female characters who can’t/don’t go around rampantly murdering people, or who need to be protected physically – as long as their agency and strength are demonstrated in other ways. In this case, Idilko’s big brave moment is to act as bait to lure some robbers for like 10 seconds. Which like….I mean, I still wouldn’t be brave enough to do it, but it was a little underwhelming.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="380291673811684238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2144397859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2144397859" />
    <a title="Tweebs♥️ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35431290-tweebs"><img alt="Tweebs♥️ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600454813p2/35431290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2144397859?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tweebs♥️ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tweebs♥️ " href="/user/show/35431290-tweebs">Tweebs♥️ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2144397859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7074810566575108593"><blockquote>
  <i>"You find me ugly, don't you?" she said.<br/> "Hideous." he said. " A hag of a woman." <br/>Another peal of laughter met his words. Brishen wilted, relieved she took no insult in him so bluntly validating her assumption.<br/>"And you," he said. "You don't think me a handsome man?"<br/>"Had you crawled out from under my bed when I was a child, I would have bludgeoned you to death with my father's mace." </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>dear future husband</b>, if we don’t have this type of relationship then you’ll need to take notes from this book.</span>
  <span id="freeText7074810566575108593" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"You find me ugly, don't you?" she said.<br> "Hideous." he said. " A hag of a woman." <br>Another peal of laughter met his words. Brishen wilted, relieved she took no insult in him so bluntly validating her assumption.<br>"And you," he said. "You don't think me a handsome man?"<br>"Had you crawled out from under my bed when I was a child, I would have bludgeoned you to death with my father's mace." </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>dear future husband</b>, if we don’t have this type of relationship then you’ll need to take notes from this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509504385ra/24328495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Might as fact, I'll demand a re-do on our relationship and our first meet better be as beautiful and moving as Brishen and Ildiko's. Like, so beautiful and moving that our love story gets shared among millions of people and we become a hashtag. <br><br><s>look at me putting all this pressure on a non existent dude for a non existent love life </s><br><br>I've been putting off writing this review for the longest time and well....I have my reasons, okay?? We'll just blame school because I blame it for everything. For example, my dark circles and the fact that I don't get the 8 hour required sleep. So, what made me write this? Other than the fact that I had to google kittens to give me some motivation, but <b> I needed you guys to know how much I adore this book</b>. <br><br><i>Radiance</i>, was a pleasant surprise. I found myself completely enthralled by the characters. I would adopt them in a heartbeat but like I can't even afford books right now so they kind of have to wait awhile. I never expected to pick this book up and discover it to be so addicting and enjoyable. I tried to read as slow as possible but honestly I'm not guilty about reading this in one sitting. <br><br><s>i'm actually guilty about neglecting my hmwrk but i'm a procrastinator anyway. I'm supposed to do these things. It's the only requirement of being a full time procrastinator.</s> <br><br><br>Let's break down my thoughts about this book?? <br><br><br><b>
  <u>THE PLOT</u>
</b><br><br>► <u>
  <i>What's it about???</i>
</u> Well, It's about these two characters, Brishen and Ildiko, who are in an arranged marriage to form a political alliance between the Human and Kai kingdoms. Both characters do not bring any significance to their own kingdoms hence why this marriage was formed. They were brought together by their own kingdoms but will discover they are destined for each other. You think it's going to be a happy book about love? Nah, not even close. Well, it is about love and also a kind of a typical plot with conflict, drama, and a bit of magic but yet so refreshing at the same time, does that make any sense? Read it and find out :)<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“This should never have happened, Brishen. We were unimportant, you and I. We weren't supposed to mean anything to anyone."<br>"Woman of day," he said slowly. "You mean everything to me.” </i>
</b><br><br><br>►Alright guys......Do you ever just read a book and you're so consumed by the characters that you forget to focus on the actual plot??? <br><br>► Yup that was me :) <br><br>► I realized how consumed I was and thought, <i>"let me take a step back and actually focus on the plot" </i>. I did that and found it to be a bit.....lacking and not as developed BUT THIS PROBLEM DIDN'T EVEN BECOME A PROBLEM UNTIL I PULLED MYSELF AWAY AND TRIED FOCUSING ON THE PLOT !! I tell you, these characters are that captivating. <br><br>►But I loved how the author showed us that appearances don't matter; it's the inside that does. You don't have to be with someone pretty, because honestly what's the point? I rather be with someone ugly with a beautiful heart than someone who is pretty with an ugly heart. And you'll learn that lesson in this book because I did. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>“She made him strong; she made him weak, and in that moment, she nearly put him on his knees. ”</i>
</b><br><br><br><u><b>THE COVER:</b> </u><br><br>► Honestly, the biggest turn off. <br><br>►I was NOT into it. I was NOT feeling it. <br><br>►But listen, I'm a changed person now and I'll get to that shortly so stay tuned !! <br><br><b>
  <i>“I'm serious, Brishen. Promise me you'll not get yourself killed or maimed out there."<br>"I can't make that promise, Ildiko, but I can swear to do my best to come back with all arms and legs attached."<br>She frowned. "Your head too, if you please."<br>Brishen laughed then. "My head too.” </i>
</b><br><br><br><b>
  <u>THE CHARACTERS</u>
</b><br><br>► oh my gracious <br>► oh my goodness<br>► oh my gosh <br>► oh my lord<br>► OH MY GOD <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509504060ra/24328477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► I think I should be okay now because oh my gawd what did i sign myself up for?? I think I loved these characters more than my own siblings. I never expected to invest so many feelings into this book like excuse me, is there something on my forehead that says <i>"I love to suffer" ?? </i> because wow i'm not complaining. I suffered beautifully. <br><br>►Between us, if you're reading a book and it fails to make you feel like you didn't know what your life was before these characters came in then do me a favor and toss that book aside. It's not doing its job. You know what book will fulfill that ??? This book. <br><br>► Let's start with my child, Brishen. Can we have a moment of silence and just appreciate him?? I've been an absolute sucker for Brishen since the beginning because he is <b> funny, loyal, courageous, kind, understanding, friendly, kick ass, and 1000 other qualities which would take me 3 years to list </b>. He is a precious blueberry muffin and I'd totally eat him. <i>( That was such a bad joke pls ignore me)</i>. He is perfect in every way and just.........more book boyfriends. I should just become a collector because that's all I do in my life. I just collect book boyfriends left and right. <br><br>► Now Ildiko................this woman. She was like a breath of fresh air and also <b> loyal, hilarious, bad ass, sarcastic, and understanding</b>. I loved her from beginning to end. She wasn't those typical characters that just chill and only exist to be annoying af. I just.........I've adopted to many characters but one isn't going to hurt, right??? <br><br>► Anhuset and serovek are those types of characters where you can't even prepare for them like good luck. Yeah I'm serious that's all I'm giving you about them. Just Good luck. #ishipthem #what #whosaidthat #notme<br><br>►Honestly, the author will make you fall in love with each character as you progress through the story. It's not like you were given a choice. I didn't even make it past chapter 1 before I declared my love for these characters. <br><br><u>
  <b>me to me after finishing this book</b>
</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509639748ra/24344195.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Sleep here each day, Ildiko.” A sweet warmth suffused her. She entangled her legs with his and hugged his arm to her waist. “As you wish. Just don’t steal the blankets.” </i>
</b><br><br><br>Well, that's it folks. That's all I can say about this book unless you have 3 years to spare because I can go on :) But I hope you will give this book a chance and maybe love it more than me…...but that’s unlikely ;p Now, leave me be while I go cry about Brishen and how I need him in my life like a fish needs water.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7074810566575108593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15747496874968127611"><br/><b>6 BRISHEN stars</b><br/><br/>A simple as it sounds, I call dibs, ladies! LOL<br/><br/>This Kai Prince is simply...dear God<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462456746ra/18999758.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462456746i/18999759.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>There's nothing I didn't love here - <b>the plot, the characters, the descriptions, the action, the LOVE, the attraction greater than the superficial features..."bigger than life love story" between two individuals who couldn't be more different, physically, in kinship, in culture, in everything that distinguished them they found the connection beyond it all.</b><br/><br/><i>An arranged marriage.<br/>An alliance between two</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15747496874968127611" style="display:none"><br><b>6 BRISHEN stars</b><br><br>A simple as it sounds, I call dibs, ladies! LOL<br><br>This Kai Prince is simply...dear God<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462456746ra/18999758.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462456746i/18999759.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There's nothing I didn't love here - <b>the plot, the characters, the descriptions, the action, the LOVE, the attraction greater than the superficial features..."bigger than life love story" between two individuals who couldn't be more different, physically, in kinship, in culture, in everything that distinguished them they found the connection beyond it all.</b><br><br><i>An arranged marriage.<br>An alliance between two kingdoms.</i><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Arranged marriages were the fate of nearly all aristocratic Gauri women, each one made for power, for trade, for good of country.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Ildiko.</i><br> A young Gauri royal member set of to become a wife to a KAI prince. She's become a duchess, a Kai hercegese. BUT her position as a spare will remain the same.<br><br><i>Brishen</i><br>A KAI Prince, a younger son.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>He never imagined an arranged marriage with a human woman to seal a war and trade alliance between Bast-Hardis and Gaur.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>what started off as an <b>obligation - where both parties find the other hideous and ugly,<br><blockquote><b><i>The physical differences between human and Kai were obvious and in some ways, extreme...her acceptance helped her look beyond his startling appearance to the man himself. She'd held tight to that philosophy: see past the surface to the tides below.</i></b></blockquote></b><br>they have to adjust and learn about each other, their cultures, traditions, different and unique way od conduct<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"We're growing used to each other. My kin will grow used to you and you to them as well."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>the interactions between Ildiko and Brishen are based on mutual acceptance that goes beyond the appearance<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The contrast of gray skin and black nails against hers emphasized their physical differences, yet sorrow was sorrow.<br><br>Dreadful in appearance, lethal in combat, Brishen was all that was cordiality and dignified royalty in every interaction with her.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>expanded into a keenship and a sense of acceptance that went deep even if the outside features spoke against it, <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>She was ugly; she was beautiful, and she was his. "My Ildiko."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>then friendship,<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"..I think we all seek companionship, wife. Sometimes it's physical; sometimes it's much more....Loneliness is an empty void. We look for that friend in the light....<br>Will you be that for me, Ildiko? That beacon in the void?"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br> then comfort and understanding <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Something flared between them, a sense of camaraderie, of belonging.<br><br>While Brishen didn't find her beautiful, it was obvious to him the Gauri men did. Still, he didn't regret this union. Ildiko was unique and witty, and he enjoyed her company.<br><br>An intuitive sense of the vibrant soul and great heart that lay behind the ugly exterior?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>only to be revealed as a deep mutual loving and compassion.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I will conquer kingdoms for you if you but ask it of me, Ildiko."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>they share a mutual admiration for each other that grows each step of their destined way together and that admiration runs deep...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>While Ildiko had the heart of a warrior, she was untrained, untried, and unprepared to fend off an attack from a determined assasin. He'd lay down his life for her, protect her with sword and axe, teeth and claws if necessary.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>even when they are trialed by their differences in a constant battle of doubts, trials and fails, the fact that they have grown into each other seeking comfort and a sense of belonging can't escape them...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm not human, wife."<br>"But you're still mine, husband."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>so when the boundaries of friendship and comfort turn into the desire interwoven inside of them from the most honest and purest of places, the want and the need is undeniable...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I am no poet possessing honeyed words...but you have always known me to be forthright with you."<br>"I want you, Ildiko. Want to sink so deep into you that neither of us will know where one ends and the other begins."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453986722ra/17900545.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"What is it, Ildiko? What do you see?"<br>"My beautiful husband. I see radiance."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399627461ra/9576505.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"What will I teach you?"<br>"Patience. <br>Endurace.<br>Ecstasy.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462456746i/18999760.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462456746i/18999761.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>His need for her ran like molten streams just under his skin</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418016528ra/12640700.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>BUT just when they found each other within each other, the malice doesn't sleep, there are devious plans forged in front of their eyes, in their presence...just to unleash the danger that would destroy them all...<br><br><b>Simply phenomenal story, captivating characters</b>...I am eager to continue with <b>Brishen and Ildiko's story</b> as they are about to <b>encounter another task to dwell upon, survive and find each other all over again...in the chaos and mess of an unleashed dread...</b><br><br>BR with <b>milady Denise</b><br><br>special thanks to <b>Kazy</b> who generously pointed out this book to me...<br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_1390431521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1390431521" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1390431521?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Angela by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/46375243-cory">Cory</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1390431521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2079104333847460642">Wow. Just wow. I'm so glad that Kaynan urged me to read this RIGHT NOW. This is an incredibly good book, and I had a really hard time putting it down to deal with (very necessary) tasks, like: getting kids ready for school, helping with homework, making dinner, bedtime routines, and playing with the kids...Oops.<br/><br/>The very best part of this book is the two main characters, Brishen and Ildiko (how the hell do you pronounce her name?? Every time I see it in the text I took 5 seconds to try to reason </span>
  <span id="freeText2079104333847460642" style="display:none">Wow. Just wow. I'm so glad that Kaynan urged me to read this RIGHT NOW. This is an incredibly good book, and I had a really hard time putting it down to deal with (very necessary) tasks, like: getting kids ready for school, helping with homework, making dinner, bedtime routines, and playing with the kids...Oops.<br /><br />The very best part of this book is the two main characters, Brishen and Ildiko (how the hell do you pronounce her name?? Every time I see it in the text I took 5 seconds to try to reason it out before moving on. I'm quite sure I'm saying it wrong in my head).<br /><br />Brishen is the <i>spare</i> prince of the Kai. Ildiko is the niece of the Gauri king. Both are unimportant in their respective kingdoms. Left aside to be used as pawns in some negotiation or another. A negotiation, it turns out, that finds them wed to each other.<br /><br />I don't think there's anything particularly <i>spectacular</i> about either character alone. They're both nice, kind, honorable people. They face life rather than bemoaning their circumstances. They don't take their frustrations out on those that are undeserving of them, and the genuinely try to be <b>good</b>. In fact, it's kind of hard to find a flaw with either of them. But that's okay. Because the true love that I have here is them <b>together</b>. <br /><br />Together, Brishen and Ildiko are amazing. They are one-hundred-percent honest with each other. Their love is built on friendship and mutual care and respect, not attraction and the desire to have sex at every other turn. They learn each other, they are honest with each other, and - to start - they find each other hideous. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"You find me ugly, don't you?"<br /><br />Brishen had faced abominations on the battlefield without flinching, leapt into the thick of the fighting against creatures born from the nightmares of lesser demons. Not once had he been tempted to run away in fear. Now, his leg muscles rippled with the urge to flee. He clenched his teeth instead, prayed he wouldn't start a war with their newest ally and answered honestly.<br /><br />"Hideous," he said. "A hag of a woman."<br /><br />Another peal of laughter met his words. Brishen wilted, relieved she took no insult in him so bluntly validating her assumption. He didn't even know her name, but he liked her and didn't wish to hurt her. Assured she wasn't planning to flounce off and send a pack of offended relatives after him, he turned the same question on her.<br /><br />"And you," he said. "You don't think me a handsome man?"<br /><br />She shrugged. "I've only seen your hands and eyes. For all I know, you're hiding the face of a sun spirit in that hood."<br /><br />Brishen scoffed at the idea. "Hardly." He'd never lacked female company, and his people thought him well-favored. Certainly nothing as wretched as a sun spirit. He slid the hood back to his shoulders.<br /><br />The woman's eyes rounded. She inhaled a harsh breath and clasped one hand to her chest. Her mollusk skin went a far more attractive shade of ash. She remained silent and stared at him until he raised a hand in question. "Well?"<br /><br />She exhaled slowly. The space between her eyebrows stitched into a single vertical frown line. "Had you crawled out from under my bed when I was a child, I would have bludgeoned you to death with my father's mace."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />How could I *not* love them after that meet-cute??<br /><br />Because their marriage is to secure and alliance there's obviously some other machinations going on in the book, but really this is the story about Brishen and Ildiko growing to love each other. Two outcasts that find true love and companionship in each other. <br /><br />The slow burn of their budding relationship was so refreshing. Without attraction and sexual desire mucking up the works, they form their relationship organically - on friendship and respect. Who'd have thought that could work so well? Don't get me wrong, I love the attraction and sexual tension as much as anyone (and you get some of that here too, don't worry), but can't there be a time and place? Can't our characters have something more to fall back on than ... well, their backs?<br /><br />This book says, emphatically, YES!<br /><br />I said that this is really the story of Brishen and Ildiko's falling in love, and that's probably where my only real complaint lies, too. I love their story. A LOT. But I do wish that we'd gotten more of the world, more of the threatening war, more of the politics, more of the cultures of both peoples. <br /><br />And then we get to the ending. After such a sweet moment between our heroes, that epilogue hit me over the head and shocked the hell out of me! What? Where did that come from?? Things just got real!<br /><br />I NEED to see what happens next. <i>Eidolon</i>, please. Gimme.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2079104333847460642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3242790617" class="readable"
              >

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1851213394" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851213394" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1851213394?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=urr-botms">urr-botms</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=2017-romance-reading-challenge">2017-romance-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1851213394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12040254737995701416"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I read this book for the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unapologetic Romance Readers</a>' New Years 2017 Reading Challenge. For more info about what this is, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/14473082-new-years-2017-reading-challenge' rel='nofollow noopener'>click here</a>.<br/><br/><br/><br/>We read this as part of a monthly "theme read" in my romance book group. The subject was slow-burn romances. I <i>love </i>slow-burn romances, <i>when </i>it's done well, that is, and when I saw that this was a fantasy romance, I was even more excited. More so, because most of my friends loved it, and one of them compar</span>
  <span id="freeText12040254737995701416" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I read this book for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers" rel="nofollow noopener">Unapologetic Romance Readers</a>' New Years 2017 Reading Challenge. For more info about what this is, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/14473082-new-years-2017-reading-challenge" rel="nofollow noopener">click here</a>.<br><br><br><br>We read this as part of a monthly "theme read" in my romance book group. The subject was slow-burn romances. I <i>love </i>slow-burn romances, <i>when </i>it's done well, that is, and when I saw that this was a fantasy romance, I was even more excited. More so, because most of my friends loved it, and one of them compared the author to R. Lee Smith.<br><br><br><br>Don't be thinking that this is alien-smut, though. For most of the book, it's actually quite chaste. Ildiko is a "Gauri" human woman and Brishen is a "Kai" man (something I imagined as being like a "dark elf"). The two are lesser nobility, and are being married to forge an alliance between their kingdoms.<br><br><br><br>They actually meet first in a garden, and both are charmed by each other despite the animosity between their two races. They're delighted, then, when it turns out later that the "stranger" they each had met is actually their husband/wife-to-be, respectively. Even though neither finds the other attractive (though both are considered the ideal form of beauty for their own race but ugly to each other's races), they know that they've got a good deal, and appreciate one another's humor and kindness.<br><br><br><br>The best thing about RADIANCE, for me, is that it's about two very kind, humorous, <i>nice </i>people falling in love with one another not because of their looks but because of their deeds. The relationship that develops between them is at first amicable and platonic. When Ildiko goes to court with Brishen, he's impressed by her bravery and her determination to conform to his people's ways, and in return attempts to help her get through the worst ordeals (like eating scarpatine pie - picture a chicken pot pie, only made with giant scorpions instead of chicken, and the scorpion is still alive). Draven also portrays culture shock well, with both characters feeling lonely and frustrated with their <i>faux pas</i>.<br><br><br><br>What killed this book a bit for me was the last 10% when something sad happens. I think that probably put some people off the book - especially those who like super happy, picture perfect endings. It didn't bother me as much, but it was enough to put a damper on my previously untempered joy. One of the people in the romance group also pointed out that the epilogue will confuse you if you don't want to read the sequel, as it doesn't really add anything to the story (which ends on an HEA note) and is pretty much solely intended to set up the sequel.<br><br><br><br>I really enjoyed RADIANCE, though. The characters and the writing were great, and for a story where pretty much <i>nothing </i>happens except for the characters interacting with each other - this is largely a character-driven piece - the world and the characters are developed enough that it was still a interesting read. Anyone who is tired of romance novels where the characters act like assholes to one another should pick up RADIANCE.<br><br><br><br> 4 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12040254737995701416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EUuCnKghDvIogvQWRkpATwXkJEP0I2P40RAqnlCc5Hc7EDeCUAxHNyWDavu6RHp4Rz6UyaiROch+5rAEGaVwxg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OCX6EwoypSnpNh4vpEFgFiwefdGecaDX2N/jWrDj5mMSfk8N8h/s7OQ3gMJYT1ohbsTNW8LD+ud3KXnA+dpy0g==')})
  }
//]]>
